No sophomore slump here. Beth & Joe have hit their stride and perhaps are even more in tune with working together on the second go around.<br /><br />A classy choice of songs have been selected, previously recorded by Aretha Franklin, Etta James, Billie Holiday, Donnie Hathaway, Lucinda Williams, Buddy Miles, Tina Turner, Slackwax, Melody Gardot, and Nina Simone.  From big band sounds, to sultry ballads, to balls out growl and howl, to French inspired with Arlan Schierbaum on accordion. Somehow the diversity of the songs are tied together to make a cohesive whole. Anton Fig gives a powerhouse performance on drums with the rest of the excellent band Blondie Chaplin and Carmine Rojas rounding everything out.<br /><br />Vintage songs and in a sense vintage recording as well. Producer Kevin Shirley's method of recording live in the studio with the entire band playing together is the antithesis of so much of today's manipulated and computerized music. This band is interacting with each other and having FUN - and you can hear it in the music! Later in the process the horns by Lee Thornburg and Ron Dziubla are added as well as the strings by Jeff Bova which just takes everything to yet another level.<br /><br />Beth Hart not only has an effing astounding voice, but the ability to truly connect with the material and make it her own, then communicate the emotion behind it. Joe Bonamassa augments the songs and compliments Beth's vocals perfectly with tasteful guitar work that is restrained in places and in some places he really lets loose. He shines on the solo at the end of I Love You More than You'll Ever Know with bluesy, soulful work.<br /><br />Stunning record. Brilliantly done. One of the best albums of the year. A big sassy bitch of an album!

B00BYISQTO|5.0|The National is one of those groups that you don't quite understand at first, yet with time their music becomes something personal and affecting. With every album they expand their sound, dig a little bit deeper, and unearth some treasures that leave you speechless. Trouble Will Find Me is exactly what you would expect from this group: tight musicianship, haunting atmosphere, and melodies that stick with you long after the record has finished playing.<br /><br />The good news for fans is that this isn't a radical departure from what's come before. If you've enjoyed anything from their previous albums then you'll feel right at home here among the band's trademarks. Matt Berninger's delicate baritone voice glides effortlessly over every cut, from the tender opening of \\"I Should Live in Salt\\" to the creepy introspection of \\"Demons\\". He remains the group's driving force and instantly pulls you into the dark and sordid affairs of these songs. The band members themselves are solid as always and each one adds a subtle yet indelible touch every step of the way. Repeated listens reveal just how intricate these songs are and you'll begin to hear flourishes and small production touches that had previously remained hidden. Musically it's a bit more fast-paced, akin to their earlier work and the sequencing ensures that ballads like \\"Fireproof\\" and \\"This Is the Last Time\\" are mixed nicely with driving anthems like \\"Sea of Love\\" and \\"Graceless\\". The mixing is well-balanced and thankfully isn't too compressed. The record has some breathing room and continues to give off an aura of intimacy that makes it easy to get lost in the atmosphere.<br /><br />While The National hasn't changed up their sound in any significant way, they've proven to be great at what they do and Trouble Will Find Me is a stellar addition to their impressive body of work. It lacks some of the unpredictability and obtuse arrangements that made High Violet so incredible but it's comforting to find the band staying fresh and building upon what's come before. This is a great treat for dedicated fans and a welcome springboard for curious newcomers. Highly recommended.g fresh and building upon what's come before. 0143120581|4.0|I really liked this book. The story is well-written and the topic was riveting.  I think it's rare to read a memoir that is so brutally honest and sincere.  Ms. Chua knows how to build a story.  She doesn't try to sugar coat anything and she bares her soul, showing her successes as well as her failures. Plus, her daughters helped her edit the book, so the perspective isn't one-sided.  Sometimes I laughed out loud and felt bad for Ms. Chua.  Other times I wondered if she was crazy.<br /><br />For anyone who thinks this is a guide to Chinese parenting: please stop.  It isn't.  This is one mother's story. There are some cultural similarities amongst mothers of a given culture, sure; but it is ridiculous to think that all mothers of any ONE culture parent the same exact way.  I did see some commonalities between her parenting and the way my parents (both Chinese) raised me.  However, despite the fact that my mom did assign me extra homework and sign me up for piano lessons, she also allowed me to go to sleepovers, let me sing/act in plays, and never (I mean never) criticized me.  She was strict, but never mean.<br /><br />If you are interested in one Chinese mother's experience raising children, you will have front row seats through this highly entertaining book.  It's easy to criticize other parents when you're sitting in a comfortable arm chair, but what parent is perfect?  Whether you agree with Ms. Chua or not, you have to admit the lady is brave to bare her self-admitted flawed parenting techniques to a world that loves to judge and criticize others (especially parents).  I respect Ms. Chua for doing that.

0385349947|5.0|Lean In is thought-provoking, inspiring, motivating, honest, funny, and fair. Every chapter made me think. Sometimes I had to put down the book in wonder because I identified so much with what she was saying.  It was eye-opening.  When she talked about being called &#34;bossy&#34; as a child because she liked to organize and lead, I saw myself, too.  I nodded in agreement with her observation that traits admired in men are discouraged in women.  The little boy who leads and organizes is seen as a born leader with initiative.  The little girl who does the same is seen as a bossy know-it-all who doesn't play well with others.  How true, and sad.<br /><br />I've read some criticisms about the book and it seems to me those people fall into a few categories: (a) they didn't read the whole book, or didn't get it; (b) they were getting defensive as a result of their own insecurities, thereby twisting her words, or (c) they were dismissive of her advice because they saw her as &#34;privileged.&#34;  I think people need to remember that Ms. Sandberg didn't grow up with tons of money, pampered in a lavish cocoon.  She worked hard to get where she is, and is able to afford some what she has in part due to her hard work (and in part due to her husband's hard work).  This book isn't about how to become like her.  It's about how to find your own strength and value as a woman (as a person), when you're a part of a society that constantly encourages you to follow others instead of lead.<br /><br />Ms. Sandberg advocates choice and equality above all, not one way all women should be. I think the most ''controversial'' part of her book is that instead of only blaming men or putting all the responsibility on men to ''give'' women equality, she also suggests ways that women can empower and help themselves and each other.  I found that empowering and validating! I think hers is a much needed voice in modern dialogues about gender equality in the home and in the workplace. It's also insightful for and applicable to men too. Ultimately, one of her main messages is TEAMWORK.  Women's place in society and in business cannot change unless we roll up our sleeves, and also go to work with our male allies.  It is not an us vs. them game - that just sets us up for failure (something that Dr. Martin Luther King, Jr. also warned against).  Ms. Sandberg explains exactly HOW to work toward equality based on personal experience and multiple psychological and social studies - she doesn't just theorize. Plus she gives great business advice, which is very helpful.<br /><br />I loved this book and have recommended it to all the women in my life.  I've even recommended it to some men.  It is highly informative as well as entertaining!  How often does that happen?  I think you should check it out.ghtful for and applicable to men too. B00C061I3K|5.0|\\"A light but polished, elegant record whose robotic vocals would hold expressiveness and emotion.\\"- Thomas Bangalter.<br /><br />Random Access Memories, the fourth album from Daft Punk, is eclectic, innovative, engaging and very interesting to listen to. If you're expecting just another EDM cd, you'd be disappointed.  If not, you're gonna love it.  Lending their cache to the effort are singing legend Paul Williams, Giorgio Moroder, Panda Bear, Pharrell Williams, Chilly Gonzales and music icon Nile Rodgers, whose fingerprints are all over the place.  The decision to take it back to a classic early 80's mix of disco and smooth jazz-styles featuring session musicians is a good one.  This cd sounds... alive!  You'd almost think the late Roger and Larry Troutman from ZAPP! were looking down on them while they made it.  With 13 tracks, each one has something special, something to make you want to explore and not just play them.  Also makes it hard to pick out some to highlight.<br /><br />01- Give Life to Back to Music: if you're of that certain age, soon as you hear the drums, rhythm guitar, bass and party chatter flowing through this one you'll want to lace up your roller skates and hit the rink!  And you won't take them off until the cd's finished.<br /><br />03- Giorgio by Moroder: a slice of musical history with disco icon Giorgio Moroder as he outlines his music journey through snippets mixed in with the beats and rhythms.  Most interesting is how he was recorded with three distinct mics- including two from the 60s, 70s- to reflect his decades-spanning career.<br /><br />05- Instant Crush with Julian Casablancas: One of my faves, but the music is almost spot on from another 80s tune, \\"Eye In The Sky\\" by Alan Parsons Project, right down to the filtering of Casablanca's voice (Thanks to Eric Shepard and Booky McGee for helping me out with that).<br /><br />06- Lose Yourself to Dance with Pharrell Williams: Not really into his singing, but this one is one of the best tracks!  And yeah, those are real hand claps you're hearing.<br /><br />07- Touch featuring Paul Williams: Williams also wrote the lyrics.  Ever-shifting and psychedelically complex, it's rumored to be based upon a Brian de Palma film that Williams also starred in and scored.  Reminds you in a lot of ways of the Beatles, especially \\"A Day in the Life\\".<br /><br />08- Get Lucky with Pharrell Williams: the first single release.  It's what a night out is all about, not just what the title's metaphor suggests.<br /><br />09- Beyond: starts out with string sweeps like a movie score, but switches into a keyboard/guitar rhythm straight from Michael McDonald's classic \\"I Keep Forgetting\\".<br /><br />11- Fragments of Time with Todd Edwards: another infective, jazzy upbeat tune to nod your head to.  Singing reminds you of Justin Timberlake or Jon B.<br /><br />13- Contact: starting with a recording from the Apollo 17 mission describing a strange object witnessed in space to set the tone, there's some shades of TRON: Legacy here, but what really makes it are the drums as the song progresses and peaks.<br /><br />This one is completely unexpected and that's part of what makes it so much fun!
